And if I didn't like it, well it's good intestinal ruffage for me.<br /><br />The story I read followed this basic pattern and dialogue, all involving the overused word \\"crap\\" and it's conjugations:<br /><br />\\"He's looking at me. Crap. I'm looking at him. Double crap. He cocked his head (also overused) to the side. Triple crap. Oh my, his eyes are so grey (this is repeated about 670,983 times). Quadrupled crappity crapping crap playing craps while crapping on the crappy crapping crapper.\\"<br /><br />The main protagonist, Anastasia Steele, likes to say \\"crap\\" a lot. It made me have to go to the bathroom. And I ATE this book?<br /><br />I wonder again what makes everyone praise this thing and why it is such a hit. It's incredibly pedestrian, sophomoric and trite. Why does this sell? I feel like the truly good books are small and sparse pines on a mountain face and all of the popular ones of today are avalanches that consume them. The good ones get flushed away by the wuthering of the mediocrity monster.<br /><br />I found myself furrowing my brow in confusion while reading it. Where is the brilliance? What is so enchanting about it? Why, why, why was this such a big hit? I tried in vain to find something magical or even mildly interesting about the contents and characters, but found I had more fun playing the drinking game whenever the main character gasped about Grey's grey eyes. I need a new liver. Thanks.<br /><br />Of course, I could just be a snob and much too uncompromising, having read Jane Eyre and several other classics shortly before I picked up this cannon fodder... AHHH, I mean BOOK. So I may be a snob. Caviar and crumpets, Jeeves... yes, do bring some, won't you? Thank you, dearest.<br /><br />But I doubt I'm a snob. I just don't like fast food literature. Don't be confused - the book itself isn't fast food (doesn't taste like it, anyway). I'm just saying the contents are for the masses who like dumb, easy reading.<br /><br />If you want to read literature that is the equivalent of the overpriced, frou frou sounding dishes at restaurants for the rich, find a classics list online. Read them. They are classics for a reason. And you won't even have to leave a gratuity.<br /><br />This review is long enough. Crap. It's getting late. Double crap. I have to go. Triple crap!<br /><br />Bathroom here I come.

0307592731|5.0|This is an exceptional memoir written by a woman who had embarked on a grand adventure traversing the Pacific Crest Trail alone almost 17 years earlier. Along the way she faces the demons that have haunted her during those years.  Strayed's writing is phenomenal, exposing a brutal honesty about her willingness to unearth the truth about herself and the often disfunctional behaviors she had engaged in to avoid her grief before the trek.  Highly recommended.

B0000CABBW|5.0|I found this movie to be quite stunning, not only visually, but emotionally, as well.  It was quite touching and moving, and I found myself very much connected to the lead actress, Pai.  Learning about indigenous cultures and their struggles to maintain their traditions and morals in an ever-changing modern world really helped me to see the depth of this film.  For me, the inner turmoil of the Maori tribe that is depicted on screen is the result of them trying to hold on tightly to the foundation that their ancestors built.  I think there is meant to be a subdued understanding that modern ways-of-life are gradually taking hold of their own private society.  The only things you see in the film to suggest this is the music blaring from a stereo and the graphics on the clothes of the children.  Basically, this is telling us that there is a world outside of the Maori civilization that is threatening to take over if they are not able to fight it off.<br /><br />The young actress, Keshia Castle-Hughes, gave an Oscar-worthy performance as Pai, a young Maori girl whose mother and twin brother died during birth, and whose father left her with her grandparents so that he could venture out on business.  Pai's grandfather, Koro, is very resentful of the fact that there is no male heir to take his place as leader of his Maori community.  To remedy the situation, he starts a school to teach the young boys of the community the ways of the Maori.  Pai tries to take part in the education, but is harshly refused because she is a girl.  Pai never gives up the fight for equality, and is encouraged by her loving grandmother.  Although her grandfather also loves her very much, he is unable to see past her gender to see that she does, indeed, possess the perfect leadership qualities he has been searching for.<br /><br />I watched this movie as an assignment for class, but I am taking much more away from it than that.  It really opened my eyes to the differences between my modern world andthe modern world of indigenous tribes.  I give this film two big thumbs up and I recommend it to everyone.

0307949486|2.0|A quick read of the first chapter and the generally rave reviews proved to be enough to goad me into picking up The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo with the serious intent of joining that illustrious and ever expanding club boasting of its literary greatness.  Admittedly, all the ingredients of a great story and page-turning experience were there: a disgraced journalist offered a chance at redemption, and revenge, through the mysterious offer of a retired businessman, etc.  What strikes me, now that I take the time to look back on the book in its entirety, is how poorly these components were executed and utilized.  I was left wondering if I had missed something, anything which explained why the novel didn't \\"come alive\\" for me as it had for so many others while only the The New York Times review made me feel sane for not gushing hyperbole over Larsson's work.  I figured a million Swedes couldn't be wrong but, as it turns out, I was.<br /><br />It may be somewhat of a misnomer to use the word \\"complaints\\" as most negative things about the book are really just disappointments.  The biggest letdown was how thoroughly unsatisfying the story was.  That first chapter left the impression that a whirlwind of intrigue and mystery was due to sweep me away at any moment; instead the first 40% of the book consisted primarily of uninteresting filler about such disparate and unimportant things as what certain characters were eating for lunch, the usefulness of a certain spreadsheet program, and the technical specifications of a particular laptop.  These digressions could have been forgiven if the rest of the book were to have made up for it in even the slightest fashion, but it sadly did not.  The story is so paper thin and cliche riddled that its almost an embarrassment to say that I plowed through to the end of what could probably have been an episode of CSI: Miami.  The climax leaves the reader with very little satisfaction for having been dedicated enough to keep going, and the revelation of the villain is almost entirely predictable because the author seems to have gone out of his way to drop hints just short of describing the character as the one with the noticeable mustache, top hat, and penchant for tying things to railroad tracks.<br /><br />All of this escapes the novel's main character which is not the girl with the dragon tattoo but is rather middle-aged journalist Mikael Blomkvist who is emblematic of how flat and dense the characters are.  He is, like most everybody else in the book, a reactionary only.  There is literally nothing in the book that gives the impression that he is a skilled investigator or in any way possesses superior abilities to any other guy walking by on the sidewalk, and, as luck would have it, the story proves just how unremarkable he is.  Events happen, Blomkvist muses on it for a while and then waits until the next event takes place.  Indeed, the big break in the story comes not from Blomkvist but rather by an incredibly random and fortunate visit from his daughter who is only really mentioned at that one instant in the novel.  As I said, Blomkvist is the poster boy for the larger problem faced by all of the characters: they leave you with no reason to \\"root\\" for them.  Even the title character, who is perhaps somewhat more sympathetic, is still so thoroughly pidgeonholed that one expects the next big twist to be that she has feathers and can fly.  When so many books can offer characters, stories, and experiences that are so rich and nuanced The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo feels strangely antiquated and not with the patina of a classic quality that continues to endear so many older works to our hearts.<br /><br />I wanted so much to like this book, but the myriad disappointments were so inescapable that I found myself being annoyed with the book for significant amounts of time.  The wasted capital of all the good ideas that could have made the book truly remarkable is what ultimately sank the entire experience, though a mostly superfluous first third of the book didn't help much.  I imagine that perhaps some of the book's appeal and wild popularity in Sweden was that it touched on themes and topics very germane to that country and which are somewhat less prominent here.nce, though a mostly superfluous first third of the book didn't help much.  I imagine that perhaps some of the book's appeal and wild popularity in Sweden was that it touched on themes and topics very germane to that country and which are somewhat less prominent here.
B007OUFESC|4.0|If director David Cronenberg's early films like Videodrome and The Fly were concerned about \\"the new flesh\\", then his most recent efforts have been fascinated with \\"the new mind.\\"  It might be the drug addled world of Naked Lunch or the disturbed mind of Spider or the amoral world of Eastern Promises, but the director has gone from visceral horror into more intellectually disturbing terrain.<br /><br />And \\"A Dangerous Method\\" fits this world view quite well.  I was leery of seeing this film since it generated very mixed reviews, with some people loving it and others finding it tedious.  I liked it a lot and think the problem is that this is really two films.  On the surface everything is Victorian prim and proper.  Except for some naughty spanking scenes, the film has few Cronenbergian flourishes.<br /><br />But go one level deeper and follow what everyone is talking about and things get more disturbing.  When Carl Jung uses Freud's experimental \\"talking method\\" on a new female patient Sabrina Spielrein, we get into a world of sexual repression, adulterous affairs, mysticism versus hedonism, and hints of European Anti-Semitism on the eve of World War II.  There may also be an intellectual menage a trois going on here - with Jung as ego rebelling against superego father figure in Freud and Spielrein as id (and Vincent Cassel's hedonistic Otto Gross could serve as Libido, I guess).<br /><br />Cerebral and complex, and let's be honest, dialogue heavy in quite a few places, this is not an action packed film.  But it is an intellectually challenging and provocative multi-level film, with superb cinematography and fine performances by all the leads.<br /><br />I must admit I am a fan of director Cronenberg - but I am not blind to his faults.  He can be very distant and aloof as a director - M Butterfly was definitely not his best effort and Spider left me cold.  I found Dangerous Method challenging and involving from start to finish.  In his early film Scanners, Cronenberg had a famous scene where a human head literally explodes.  Cronenberg is still there in your head, just messing with it in an entirely new way.

B00634GHJA|4.0|I am not sure why everyone keeps saying it is the same as Dropbox or SugarSync; it is not.  That is like saying Dropbox is the same as a Windows Workgroup file share, IT IS NOT!  Dropbox is a server-client synchronization model, this product is a peer-to-peer model; these are not the same!  The difference is, one has a middle-man that is out in the cloud, and therefore limited by whatever the upload limit of your current broadband connection (Dropbox).  THIS product is a local network only sharing application, which can go as fast as your wireless can carry it to the other device or computer.  I hate to rant, but am tired of all the sheeple repeating the same mis-informed tripe!<br />This app is a good alternative for users who do not have a rooted device, and can not setup Samba. It is better than Dropbox in the respect that it is faster, and is peer-to-peer rather than having to first upload the photos to the \\"cloud\\" to share them with somebody else.  Also, it does not require the other user to have a Dropbox account, or that the other user have knowledge of using Dropbox. Ways that could make the app better are:<br />1). The ability to send a message with the URL within the app via TXT or email to somebody.  This would circumvent the issue another use mentioned about having to pop in and out of the app again just to send the URL.<br />2) Add the option of sharing any type of file, why just photos? This app could potentially share other types of files.<br />3) Make it so that the folder/file selection screen is sorted or able to be sorted.  Trying to navigate the dozens of folder the app found photos in is tedious.<br />4) Possibly add an advanced options menu to enable features like sharing on a 3G connection (temporarily and with warnings).  Or perhaps the ability to specify folders to list when sharing.

0756405890|5.0|ABOUT FIVE YEARS AGO I DECIDED TO BROADEN MY HORIZONS AND READ SOME SCIENCE FICTION AND FANTASY.  I BEGAN BY RESEARCHING NOVELS THAT WON BOTH THE HUGO AND NEBULA AWARDS IN THE SAME YEAR AND MOVED ON FROM THERE.  THE MAJORITY OF THESE AWARD WINNING NOVELS ARE SEGMENTS IN A SERIES, AND MORE OFTEN THAN NOT THE FIRST SEGMENT.  THERE ARE EXCEPTIONS, ENDERS GAME, AND SEQUEL SPEAKER FOR THE DEAD BOTH WHERE HONORED THROUGH WINNING BOTH OF THESE PRESTIGIOUS SCIENCE FICTION AND FANTASY AWARDS.  THE OTHER BOOKS IN THE SERIES WERE REMARKABLE AS WELL.  I HAVE FOUND THAT TO BE TRUE WITH MANY OF THESE SERIES, AND I AM NOW A FULLY DEDICATED SCIENCE FICTION AND FANTASY READER.<br /><br />I HAVE READ MOST OF THE GREATS.  I DEFINE GREATNESS IN THESE CLOSELY RELATED GENRES THROUGH IMMORTALITY....STORIES THAT WILL LIVE FOREVER, AND THE AUTHORS NAMES THAT ARE STAMPED TO THEM.  THERE ARE MANY TO CHOSE FROM, FOR ME IT WAS ASIMOV AND THE FOUNDATION NOVELS, DAN SIMMONS AND THE HYPERION QUARTET (PROFOUNDLY UNDER RATED) AND TO A SLIGHTLY LESSER EXTENT THE ORIGINAL FRANK HERBERT DUNE NOVELS, AND CARD'S ENDER NOVELS.  I AM LEAVING OUT SO MANY AND I WOULD BE REMISS TO LEAVE OUT TOLKIN AND THE LORD OF THE RING NOVELS WHICH ARE UPPER ECHELON HALL OF FAMERS.<br /><br />RECENTLY IN READING THROUGH THE GAME OF THRONES NOVELS, I THOUGHT GEORGE RR MARTIN MAY HAVE ESTABLISHED HIMSELF FIRMLY AT THE TOP OF THE LIST. ALL OF THAT IS NOW IN THE PAST BELONGING TO A DIFFERENT ERA, A TIME BEFORE KVOTHE WAS INTRODUCED TO THE WORLD.<br /><br />PATRICK ROTHFUSS BECAME AN IMMORTAL IN THE FIRST 100 PAGES OF THE NAME OF THE WIND.  THIS NOVEL IS THE FIRST OF A TRILOGY WHICH INVOLVES AN ENIGMATIC AND SEEMINGLY DESPONDENT INN-KEEPER WHO IS ACTUALLY A POWERFUL WIZARD OR ARCANIST.  HE IS A LEGEND, THE SUBJECT OF COUNTLESS TALES AND ADVENTURES.  HE IS ALSO PRESUMED DEAD.  EVENTUALLY A CHRONICLER IS INTRODUCED TO THE STORY AND PROCEEDS TO APPEAR IN THE INN (BY FATE OR DESIGN) AND RECOGNIZES THE FACT THAT THIS INN-KEEPER IS ACTUALLY KVOTHE, AND WITH THE HELP OF KVOTHE'S PROTEGEE, A MEMBER OF THE FAY NAMED BAST, THE IN-KEEPER IS FINALLY CONVINCED TO SET THE RECORD STRAIGHT.  HE TELLS THE CHRONICLER THAT IT WILL TAKE 3 DAYS TO TELL HIS STORY WITH COMPLETE ACCURACY, AND EACH NOVEL IN THE TRILOGY IS TO REPRESENT ONE DAY.  THERE MIGHT BE SOME CYNICS OUT THERE WHO WILL ARGUE THAT IT TAKES MORE THAN ONE NOVEL TO MAKE AN AUTHOR AN ALL TIME GREAT, AND THERE IS SOMETHING TO BE SAID FOR THAT.  ROTHFUSS WENT AHEAD AND FOLLOWED HIS MASTERPIECE WITH ANOTHER IN THE SECOND BOOK ENTITLED THE WISEMAN'S FEAR.  QUALITY TRILOGIES ARE SAID TO BE RARE.  IT TAKES SOMEONE SPECIAL TO MAKE A SEQUEL FLOW WITH THE SAME PACE AND LANGUAGE AS THE ORIGINAL.  ROTHFUSS TOOK HIS TIME IN PERFECTING THE SEQUEL.  HE WAS EAGER TO HEAR AS MUCH FEEDBACK AS POSSIBLE FROM READERS, LISTENING CAREFUL WHAT THEY WANTED MORE OF, AND EVEN WHAT THEY WANTED LESS OFF IN TERMS OF ASPECTS THAT ENDEARED THEM TO THE ORIGINAL.  THE MOST PAINSTAKING ASPECT OF THESE NOVELS IS HAVING TO WAIT FOR THE THIRD EDITION.  THE LIST OF QUESTIONS THAT BEGAN TO MOUNT FROM THE EARLIEST PAGES OF THE THE NAME OF THE WIND REMAINED AT THE CLOSE OF DAY 2 IN THE WISEMAN'S FEAR.  NAMELY HOW DID KVOTHE, A LEGEND OF EARTH SHATTERING PROPORTIONS END UP AN IN-KEEPER WHO HAS SEEMINGLY GIVEN UP ON LIFE.<br /><br />THE STORY IS INCREDIBLY COMPLEX, TO THE EXTENT THAT I WILL NOT ATTEMPT TO SUMMARIZE ANYMORE OF THE SCENE THAN I ALREADY HAVE.  WHAT I WILL SAY IS THAT THIS BOOK IS WRITTEN ON ANOTHER LEVEL.  THE NOVELS I MENTIONED EARLIER SUCH AS THE FOUNDATION, DUNE, ENDER, AND HYPERION WERE MIND BOGGLING STORIES OF THE SORT THAT IT PAINED ME TO HAVE TO PUT THE BOOKS DOWN TO MEET THE BASIC NECESSITIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES OF DAILY LIFE.  GAME OF THRONES AGAIN, AN EPOCH ENTHRALLING STORY AND CHARACTERS THAT WILL LIVE FOREVER.<br /><br />HOWEVER, IF WE ARE BEING COMPLETELY HONEST WE MUST SAY THAT PATRICK ROTHFUSS WRITES ON ANOTHER STRATOSPHERE.  FORGET CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT, DETAIL, AND DESCRIPTION WHICH HE IS HANDS DOWN THE BEST OF ANYONE IN ANY GENRE OF LITERATURE (MY HUMBLE, YET UNWAVERING OPINION).  ROTHFUSS IMAGINED AND WROTE FOR US THE FIRST TWO SEGMENTS OF WHAT SHOULD ONE DAY BE CATEGORIZED AS CLASSIC LITERATURE, MANDATORY READING FOR ENGLISH AND LITERATURE MAJORS AT ALL UNIVERSITIES.  ROTHFUSS NOT ONLY TANTALIZES US WITH A STORY IN WHICH DEMANDS EVERY OUNCE OF OUR ATTENTION, BUT HE ALSO WRITES IN A FASHION THAT MAKES WORDS READ AND APPEAR BEAUTIFUL.  THIS IS A DAY AND AGE IN WHICH A GOOD STORY OFTEN MASKS POOR TECHNICAL WRITING.  THERE ARE THOSE WHO ARE GOOD AT THE ART OF STORYTELLING BUT LACKING IN THE SKILL OF LANGUAGE.  IF ANYBODY EVER DESERVED TO BE TOLD THAT THERE NOVEL WAS THE HIGHEST QUALITY OF POETRY, MUSIC, AND LYRICAL VERSE IN MOTION, IT IS PATRICK ROTHFUSS.  HIS WORK READS AS BEAUTIFULLY AS JOHN FOWLES IN THE MAGUS.  THE FIRST TWO 2 DAYS IN ROTHFUSS'S KINGKILLER CHRONICLES ARE NOVELS THAT RAISE THE STANDARD FOR STORY TELLERS AND DEFINE AN ERA OF LITERATURE. 0307352145|5.0|Throughout history, and now more than ever, extroverts have been idolized for their behavior. Workplaces look for leaders to hire even churches encourage constant leadership from their members. Extroverts are seen as the life of the party, out going, and vibrant but where does that leave the introverts? According to research 1/3 to 1/2 of the population are introverts creating a great divide in the way we all function. The concept of introverts/ extroverts defines how we live our lives as such, and how we treat others that are not like us. This regulates how we act, how we think, and overall our personalities.<br /><br />Though extroverts are idolized, Cain shows that it is the introverts that make this world run. From Newton to Einstein, Warren Buffet to Rosa Parks this book describes how through their introverted personalities they have changed the way we view physics, economics, and civil rights among many other things. Often traits associated with being an introvert are viewed negatively in our society; no one admires the qualities of being shy, quite, to them selves, or sensitive. Cain, on the contrary, argues that both introverts and extroverts should admire such qualities whether in themselves or in others.<br /><br />If you are an extrovert Cain demonstrates that respect needs to be given to introvert, and not try and change them by throwing them into spotlight. And if you are an introvert, you should respect yourself and realize your true value and the endless possibilities that you too can change the world - even if it may be from the comfort of your room.<br /><br />Cain does an excellent job describing her research and telling stories, which leaves me, an introvert, with an oomph of respect for myself and others just like me.<br />This book is for introverts and extroverts alike. We all know introverts, we might be one, we might be married to one, have children that are introverts, work with them, or simply hangout with them. Regardless of our association Cain teaches us to value introverts and respect the people around us.<br /><br />Thank you to WaterBrook Multnomah for this free book, in exchange for this honest review.

B0050XH1H2|4.0|Vaccines sounds like everyone from Strokes, Interpol, to Heavens, The National, The Cribs to the Doves, We Are Augustines, you name it. Yet I feel like they stand alone as well. As a fan of many of the aforementioned bands, The Vaccines are a welcomed addition to my collection. I believe they are embodying a particular style and sound of a particular genre of this particular era that is obviously influenced by different bands of each era, dating back to the simplistic melodies of the fifties and sixties - so when people complain and argue that they are unoriginal, I'm not sure they have a good grasp of culture. None of these folks are completely original, only they find unique ways to express something that is already out there or on the cusp of being out there. But the way The Vaccines express this style and sound feels very genuinely emotional and personal. I feel like this is what makes bands in this genre stick out for me and I can't get enough of the Vaccines for the moment. That being said, I do believe that bands that offer or create an augmentation to the sound are creatively more admirable, influential and, in my mind, have more \\"staying\\" power. I am not sure The Vaccines really add or augment anything significantly to that point rather than just fitting comfortably within the genre. So while their tunes are stuck in my head at the moment, I would give them four stars for grasping the genre while maybe not taking it to that extra level.

1451627289|4.0|I remember when I first heard about a book on time travel and the Kennedy assassination was going to be released by Stephen King, I was overwhelmed with joy. I have always been a huge King fan and have most of his novel in first editions. This book has been one of the most interesting books I have read by King because of the way the story is told. For example, many of my friends who are long time King fans felt like they were cheated by the way the plot resolves at the end. They didn't feel like King had done justice to them after reading an 800+ page book. I feel as if I wasn't too far behind them in feeling the same way. The thing about this novel is, you have to remember that it isn't done in a way that seems supernatural like many of Kings other books. Jake, the main character, behaves just like a real person would and has normal experiences (besides time traveling of-course)throughout most part of the book. It is in this aspect however, that the book accomplishes what it was made to do. Jake is very believable and many times throughout the story you find yourself asking the same questions that Jake does. I love the fact that King was able to take such a popular science fiction idea such as time traveling, and incorporate it in a way that is believable. Jake is no super hero that is invincible, who gets away with everything simply because he already knows the future. He is a normal guy who is stuck in the past due to a promise he made to an old friend that he would stop JFK's assassination and will do anything in his power to see it done. Many times he is scared and questions his ability to perform his task, other times he feels sympathy towards Oswald because he sees a side of him that only people who were closest to him would ever see. You feel this throughout the book and that's when you realize, Jake isn't so different than us. I give this book four stars simply because I expected more from the rising action and the climax. I felt that the events leading up to November 22nd were a little TOO realistic for my taste. It was hard to read things like Jake having a normal day without nothing happening. Several pages of this or even a chapter of this would have been fine, but it was a big chunk where nothing is really happening, other than Jake spying on Oswald. I'll give King credit for making things seem so realistic, but for a fiction novel, It would of been better if more supernatural things were added. The Man with the Yellow Card was an excellent addition and it was more of those kinds of things that I felt the novel needed. Besides the beginning of the novel, the last three or two chapters were the ones I enjoyed the most. That is when all the things that make me love Stephen King came out; the supernatural, time traveling, The Green Card Man, and the very interesting ending. The fiction parts of the book is where this novel excelled. If there was more emphasis on the time travel or more development with JIMBLA or even an entirely new element, this book would have been flawless. In the end however, I greatly enjoyed this book and would recommend it for someone looking at a realistic approach at someone trying to change the past and do the impossible.to November 22nd were a little TOO realistic for my taste. It was hard to read things like Jake having a normal day without nothing happening. I'll give King credit for making things seem so realistic, but for a fiction novel, It would of been better if more supernatural things were added. Besides the beginning of the novel, the last three or two chapters were the ones I enjoyed the most. The story revolves a post-apocalyptic America and there are 12 Districts which ranks people in a class-type system. District 12 is the poor class and each District above ranks higher and higher. Protagonist Katniss Everdeen lives with her family in District 12 and hunts for food for her family with her friend Gale. Once a year, \\"The Hunger Games\\" are held throughout all 12 districts, and it involves picking 1 boy and girl between the ages of 12 and 18 to fight each other to the death and specially designed arenas. When all of the youth gathers up to be chosen, Katniss's younger sister, Prim, is chosen and Katniss steps in and volunteers to take her place. The boy on her team, Peeta, had saved her family's life from starvation so she felt guilty that she would be fighting to kill someone that saved her life. One aspect that's really unique is that you feel like you're always in Katniss's head because she thinks a million questions at once and she thinks the way a true hero does. Before these Hunger Games take place, the 24 chosen ones have to go through interviews and training for the games, and everything is shot on TV for everybody to see; so families  of the chosen ones actually watch their children die. In the arena, Katniss is very different compared to the others. She makes friends with a few of the chosen people and receives lots of help like food and medicine from sponsors; that's very rare for people in such a low district. Katniss makes her closest relationship with Peeta, and they survive by faking a love relationship with the audience. Katniss sounds her age when she's going through with this, very confused if she actually likes him or not. The ending has an amazing climax, and I'm not going to spoil it. I highly recommend checking out this book, it'll be a really quick and fun read!

Again, the Xoom displayed the wrong address but entering the correct address worked perfectly.<br /><br />-----<br /><br />There is no option to put pictures in any other folder other than the default PhotoGallery; you'll have to use another app if you want to organize your pictures on your device.<br /><br />There is no password on this app's web interface; if it's running, anyone who can figure out your IP address can upload photos or videos to your device or download any photos you have selected.  There are network scanner apps that can identify the IP addresses of every machine on a network and what ports are open on those devices.  Indeed, when I ran [[ASIN:B005VT42BS Fing - Network Tools]] on my tablet, I was able to find the open port on my phone in less than 15 seconds.<br /><br />This app is hard coded to use port 8080, which is a common alternate port for web servers and thus a frequent target for hackers.  There is no option to change the port number.<br /><br />The app is only usable if it is currently on the screen.  If you leave the app for any reason or turn off the screen, it shuts down.  That means you cannot use your phone to do anything else while transferring pictures.  At least this does limit the exposure of the device to network snooping.<br /><br />-----<br /><br />This app would be useful for transferring pictures from phone to phone, phone to tablet or any such combination, or downloading them to a computer when you don't have a cable with you (copying photos from your phone to your laptop in a coffee shop, for instance).  But the app is limited to photos and video only, uploads are rather clunky and it has some potential security issues.  If this app had the option for a password, I'd give it 4 stars.<br /><br />I would recommend [[ASIN:B004OZOTSQ WiFi File Explorer PRO]] (another former FAotD) over this app.  It lets you transfer any type of file, to and from any folder on your device, it has a configurable port number and optional password protection, it can run in the background, and it's $1 cheaper.app for any reason or turn off the screen, it shuts down.  That means you cannot use your phone to do anything else while transferring pictures. Ever the optimist, I thought that surely it would soon morph into at least a literary moth if not butterfly. Unfortunately, that was not to be.<br />Readers, if you have developed standards of quality regarding the art of writing, don't make my mistakes. Beware, and read the other negative reviews. This is possibly the most poorly crafted book I've ever read.
